    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

  <span id="freeText2301489503953370679" style="display:none">At the end of the school year, Kendra and her brother Seth find themselves racing back to Fablehaven, a refuge for mythical and magical creatures. Grandpa Sorenson, the caretaker, invites three specialists -- a potion master, a magical relics collector, and a mystical creature trapper -- to help protect the property from the Society of the Evening Star, an ancient organization determined to infiltrate the preserve and steal a hidden artifact of great power. Time is running out. The Evening Star is storming the gates. If the artifact falls into the wrong hands, it could mean the downfall of other preserves and possibly the world. Will Kendra learn to use her fairy gifts in time? Will Seth stay out of trouble?</span>

      $('edition_17902663').observe('prototip:shown', function() {
        if (this.up('#box')) {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});

      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_17902663').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_17902663').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_17902663').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();

At the end of the school year Kendra finds a kobold has infiltrated her eighth grade class. She can see mystical creatures without drinking a magical milk that is usually needed to enable humans to see such beings.   <span id="freeText620742399765972687" style="display:none"><i>Rise of the Evening Star</i>, the second book of the <i>Fablehaven</i> series is more dynamic and more complex than the first one. <div id="review_137073764" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137073764" />
    <a title="Aaron Vincent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2924544-aaron-vincent"><img alt="Aaron Vincent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360133074p2/2924544.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137073764?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aaron Vincent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aaron Vincent" href="/user/show/2924544-aaron-vincent">Aaron Vincent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2924544-aaron-vincent?shelf=ya-mg-fantasy">ya-mg-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137073764" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15460178960287604940">My first venture to the magical world of Fablehaven was truly an unforgettable one. I just couldn’t stop raving about it to every bookish person I know. Truth be told, I read Harry Potter series because a number of critics and authors compared Fablehaven to it(and yes, I just read Harry Potter this year. Please, don’t kill me.) I wanted to prolong the pleasure in reading the entire Fablehaven series so I didn’t read the 2nd book immediately after the 1st one. I finally decided to revisit Fableha</span>
  <span id="freeText15460178960287604940" style="display:none">My first venture to the magical world of Fablehaven was truly an unforgettable one. I just couldn’t stop raving about it to every bookish person I know. Truth be told, I read Harry Potter series because a number of critics and authors compared Fablehaven to it(and yes, I just read Harry Potter this year. Please, don’t kill me.) I wanted to prolong the pleasure in reading the entire Fablehaven series so I didn’t read the 2nd book immediately after the 1st one. I finally decided to revisit Fablehaven because I wanted to read something magical, just in time for the holiday season.<br /><br />The Sorenson sibling are on their last days of the the school year, but for Kendra it isn’t as easy as she thought it would be. There’s suddenly a new guy in her class and every girl thinks that he’s uber hot. Kendra thought the joke’s on her because what she sees is a boy with hideous features, someone comparable to a goblin. She realized that it was indeed a goblin and of course, she’s the only one who can see it as she’s the only one who has the ability to see past through the magical veil that deceives the normal human eye, an ability she received from the fairies on her first visit to the Fablehaven.<br /><br />Kendra, knowing that the goblin is up to something mischivous, seeked the help of her smart-mouthed, drastic younger brother, Seth. As she expected, Seth can offer nothing other than his sarcastic remarks. When a mysterious man named Errol shows up, offering his help to eliminate the goblin, they reluctantly accepts it. Kendra and Seth didn’t know that the eliminating the goblin is only the first in the chain of events that will lead them to spending another summer at Fablehaven. Another summer filled with magic, schemes, betrayals, and Seth messing up with the creatures mainly setting up a C-size battery-to-gold exchange business with the satyrs.<br /><br />What I love the most about Fablehaven is how easy it is for Brandon Mull to break, crumble, and pound the wall that separates reality and fantasy. Before I know it, I was completely suckied into the land of Fablehaven filled with both colorful and sinister creatures. The rules he set on his fictional land are just wickedly cool. Fablehaven, a magical creatures preserv e, is certainly one of those fictional places – along with Hogwarts, Camp-Half Blood, etc., – that will make you wish that they really exists. Brandon Mull really do tests and expands the boundaries of the reader’s imagination.<br /><br />Seth and Kendra is a very powerful tandem, too. I know we’ve already seen a lot of siblings whose hobby is to bicker in fiction, but Seth and Kendra by far is my favorite. They just compliment each other perfectly. Seth’s naughtiness and immaturity balances well Kendra’s goody good attitude, while Kendra’s doubts and uncertainties balances well Seth’s admirable, daredevilish bravery.<br /><br />The plot are no less superb. It was a tad bit darker than the first one but definitely more engrossing. The solution to the whoddunit mystery going on isn’t a giveaway. We’re at the same pace on unveiling the culprit as the characters in the book, unlike other fantasy novels in which we’re always two-steps ahead. The surprises hidden on Brandon Mull’s sleeve is seemingly infinite and he just keeps pulling one until the very last page. This careful plotting of the mystery produced a solidly characterized culprit. The culprit was three-dimensional, and being a huge sucker for well-characterized ‘villains’, I am satisfied.<br /><br />Fablehaven: Rise of the Evening Star is another highly imaginatve book with the perfect balance of magic, sweetness, innocence, and danger. If you love watching Disney Pixar movies, then this book is for you. I love visiting the magical creatures preserve that is Fablehaven, and I’m already looking forward to my next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15460178960287604940" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1725263224" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1725263224" />
    <a title="rachel ☾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17290119-rachel"><img alt="rachel ☾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591333266p2/17290119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1725263224?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="rachel ☾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="rachel ☾" href="/user/show/17290119-rachel">rachel ☾</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1725263224" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1350011396923053279">Usually people have a special book or a series that ‘got them into reading’. I am lucky enough to be able to say that I’ve always been a reader (which sounds like I’m bragging for some reason, but I’m not trying to). There’s not a period in my life that I can remember when I <i>didn’t</i> have a book in my hand! But with that being said, there are definitely a few series from my childhood that stand out and that played a major role in my love of books. One of those series was Mull’s <i>Fablehaven</i> saga. <br/><br/>Go</span>
  <span id="freeText1350011396923053279" style="display:none">Usually people have a special book or a series that ‘got them into reading’. I am lucky enough to be able to say that I’ve always been a reader (which sounds like I’m bragging for some reason, but I’m not trying to). There’s not a period in my life that I can remember when I <i>didn’t</i> have a book in my hand! But with that being said, there are definitely a few series from my childhood that stand out and that played a major role in my love of books. One of those series was Mull’s <i>Fablehaven</i> saga. <br /><br />God, this series is just gold! I know that for some unseeable reason it has received a lot of negativity, but this is one of the most cleverly written middle grade series out there. The characterisation is some of the best that I’ve ever read. Each and every single character - no matter how major/minor they are in the over-arching storyline - are completely fleshed out. They are all complex and three-dimensional with the perfect blend of realistic positive and negative characteristic. They set themselves apart from each other without being oddly distinctive. I love that there is a lot of subtle diversity in ethnicity and nationality, and that Mull wasn’t scared to write characters who were kind of flawed. Coulter, for example, could be caring and funny in a grandfatherly sort of way, but is also mildly sexist. He grew up in a time where sexism was much more the ‘norm’ that it is now and admits that he is sort of ‘old-fashioned’. Why this can be a little frustrating for Kendra/Grandmother/Vanessa, it makes him such a well-rounded character. He isn’t perfect because perfect people don’t exist, and Mull does this with all of his characters. I don’t know how, but not matter how long we spend with the characters. Warren - Dale’s brother - was also introduced into this novel, and I simply adore him. I love that he treats Kendra and Seth with the respect that they have earned. Also, Tanu! I really wanted to get to know him more. I just… I really, really love how Mull deals with characterisation, if you couldn’t tell. <br /><br />And the plot in this sequel was just fantastic too. The first book is a little bit introductory when you look back on it, but <i>Rise of the Evening Star</i> certainly steps up the game. It introduces us to what will be the major focus of the series (which I won’t say to avoid spoilers) and it is fast-paced and enthralling throughout the whole novel. The puzzles are realistic but still nail-bitingly paced and exciting. I loved exploring more of Fablehaven and this ‘world’. <br /><br />Overall, this book was just everything I remember it being and more. I adore Mulll’s writing. I was enraptured by the plot and fell in love with the cast all over again. I definitely plan on continuing my reread of this series. It gets my highest recommendation to any and all middle grade fans. It’s still one of my all-time favourites.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1350011396923053279" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Tyler" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/777245-tyler"><img alt="Tyler" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1200241605p2/777245.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/50163106?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tyler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tyler" href="/user/show/777245-tyler">Tyler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416957706" href="/book/show/1691582.Rise_of_the_Evening_Star">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50163106" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10748976422238073243">Kendra and Seth can't wait for the end of the school year so that they can return to visit their grandparents at Fablehaven. A few days before the school year ends, a scabby kobold appears in her class. The kobold appears normal to everybody except Kendra. With the aid of a kobold exterminator they get rid of him and are then swiftly evacuated to Fablehaven for their own safety. Once there, they find out that the Society of the Evening Star (which opposes preserves such as Fablehaven) has gotten</span>
  <span id="freeText10748976422238073243" style="display:none">Kendra and Seth can't wait for the end of the school year so that they can return to visit their grandparents at Fablehaven. A few days before the school year ends, a scabby kobold appears in her class. The kobold appears normal to everybody except Kendra. With the aid of a kobold exterminator they get rid of him and are then swiftly evacuated to Fablehaven for their own safety. Once there, they find out that the Society of the Evening Star (which opposes preserves such as Fablehaven) has gotten stronger and may have even breached Fablehaven itself.<br /><br />My Review: My goal is to read 4 books between each book of a single author that I read (does that even make sense?). With these Fablehaven books I just couldn't stop myself. In fact, Alison probably resents the books as well because I read most of the book yesterday evening. I wasn't going to go to bed until I finished it. Now onto the book, this book is once again like Harry Potter with adventures and fights against magical creatures. Of course, the kids are always more clever and tougher than the adults. There are unexpected twists and surprises, giving a very enjoyable book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10748976422238073243" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/856197-delaina?shelf=ya">ya</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14240496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11732698088975072113">I liked the sequel to Fablehaven even better than Fablehaven itself. The author was able to flesh out the characters and each gained a lot of depth.<br/><br/>I read Fablehaven last night, and the sequel, Rise of the Evening Star, tonight, so they're quick reads at 3-4 hours each. (Thank you writer's strike and sick, clingy kids who INSIST on me holding them and not minding me reading at the same time!!!) <br/><br/>They’re fantasy, not unlike Harry Potter but more infused with value of the family. No Dudley or mean </span>
  <span id="freeText11732698088975072113" style="display:none">I liked the sequel to Fablehaven even better than Fablehaven itself. The author was able to flesh out the characters and each gained a lot of depth.<br /><br />I read Fablehaven last night, and the sequel, Rise of the Evening Star, tonight, so they're quick reads at 3-4 hours each. (Thank you writer's strike and sick, clingy kids who INSIST on me holding them and not minding me reading at the same time!!!) <br /><br />They’re fantasy, not unlike Harry Potter but more infused with value of the family. No Dudley or mean aunts and uncles to contend with. And, I LOVE the reading guide at the end of the book where the author (Brandon Mull) probes the depths of reading comprehension with thought-provoking questions. <br /><br />The themes in the book are excellent too. For example, the girl is a rule-keeper and the boy is a curious mischief-maker, and one of the central themes is obedience. At the end you figure out that a measure of disobedience was necessary to set in motion the events that eventually lead to the ultimate demise of evil, which could not have happened otherwise. Fascinating!!! Book 3 comes out on my bday in April.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11732698088975072113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2657063118" />
    <a title="Donna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13244359-donna"><img alt="Donna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396758075p2/13244359.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2657063118?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna" href="/user/show/13244359-donna">Donna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13244359-donna?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2657063118" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11791085264218328385">This is youth fantasy fiction. I'm not the target audience for this book, but I am giving this 5 stars for several reasons:<br/><br/>1. it was 100% age appropriate<br/>2. it was written with kids in mind and it addressed "real kid" problems and thoughts<br/>3. the characters were children and the best thing about that was that they actually acted like children. They weren't portrayed as wiser beyond their years<br/>4. my kids would have loved this.<br/>5. it had great messages for kids of all ages<br/><br/>So 5 stars.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1929769550" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1929769550" />
    <a title="Mary ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37766180-mary"><img alt="Mary ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555156334p2/37766180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1929769550?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ♥" href="/user/show/37766180-mary">Mary ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37766180-mary?shelf=faves">faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1929769550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15174996407429508722">5/5 stars <br/><br/><b> Running toward danger is foolhardy. ... But so is closing your eyes to it. Many perils become less dangerous once you understand their potential hazards. </b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514146207ra/24754602.gif' width='200' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>If there was something I missed, it was diving back to the wonderful world of Fablehaven. And thankfully, this time, it brought more surprises than the first one. This, friends, is one of the greatest middle grade series I've ever read, partly because it contains every single mythological creature someone can hear about and partly be</span>
  <span id="freeText15174996407429508722" style="display:none">5/5 stars <br><br><b> Running toward danger is foolhardy. ... But so is closing your eyes to it. Many perils become less dangerous once you understand their potential hazards. </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514146207ra/24754602.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If there was something I missed, it was diving back to the wonderful world of Fablehaven. And thankfully, this time, it brought more surprises than the first one. This, friends, is one of the greatest middle grade series I've ever read, partly because it contains every single mythological creature someone can hear about and partly because the plot is so clever and well spun that it can keep you at the edge of your seat.<br><br>Rise of The Evening Star was the kind of book I wanted to close 2017 with. It contained unlimited adventure, brought new characters into my life, answered lots of questions the previous book had left, freaked me out a little (something I honestly didn't expect but loved) and most of all, made me savor the warmth and happiness middle grade books can bring for some reason.<br><br>First of all, I adored how the artifact plot point started to unfold bit by bit, with many possibilities and new adventures rising, and wonderful new parts of the beloved magical preserve to roam through. The writing was as always incredible, with lots of jokes to lighten the mood but also a great description of everything, and voices of characters as unique as themselves.<br><br>This book was darker than the first one, and there were a lot of moments when my jaw dropped and my heart started beating faster. I missed the innocence and whimsy of the first one, but this one was more adventurous and breathtaking and I loved that as well. I also noticed that Kendra and Seth, my children and my guides through this wonderful ongoing journey, are growing more and more accustomed to the way the preserve works, and are both growing, physically and mentally.<br><br>The new characters, most of them trainers, were a breath of fresh air as well. I am excited to get to know them all better and learn more about their pasts, their motives and their strengths and weaknesses. I also loved the appearance of new dangers to focus on, secret pathways, groves, plenty of magical artifacts and potions and the role fear and courage played in this book.<br><br>For some reason, every time I find myself talking about Fablehaven, I start blurting out how incredible it is and how much it is leaking fantastical adventures and journeys through magical forests at night, because that's just the truth.<br><br>If you want to read something that will make you smile but will also give you a ton of other emotions, will keep you busy and will also be quick and 'unputdownable', this is for you ♥ If you are a fan of good world buildings and fantasy creatures of all kinds, be sure to give this one a look. <br><br>I am excited to read the rest of the series, and I honestly wish I could have read this as a child because I would have been truly mersmerized.<br><br>Until the next review...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1512149437ra/24578448.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>~Mary ♥<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15174996407429508722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_18852120" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18852120" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/984874-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1206673369p2/984874.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18852120?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/984874-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/984874-thomas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/984874-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18852120" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11287235600552111527">Kendra and Seth return to Fablehaven to discover more of what they don't know (and that can kill them) and save the day. Seth, now a year older, is a little wiser and doesn't find himself in as much trouble, but again, it is Kendra who comes through.<br/><br/>By the way, in both books, while Kendra is the reluctant heroine, she is helped by others, so this isn't some supergirl of unlimited capabilities or powers.<br/><br/>I get the feeling, in reading these first two books in the series, that these two young advent</span>
  <span id="freeText11287235600552111527" style="display:none">Kendra and Seth return to Fablehaven to discover more of what they don't know (and that can kill them) and save the day. Seth, now a year older, is a little wiser and doesn't find himself in as much trouble, but again, it is Kendra who comes through.<br /><br />By the way, in both books, while Kendra is the reluctant heroine, she is helped by others, so this isn't some supergirl of unlimited capabilities or powers.<br /><br />I get the feeling, in reading these first two books in the series, that these two young adventurers have something more than just any old adult life ahead of them. That they will eventually become caretakers of the preserve is predictable, but I think it is more than that.<br /><br />Regardless, this read is much like its predecessor and stands alone surprisingly well, not needing to depend upon the first book. Regardless, I eagerly await the next installment in the series.<br /><br />This book is actually better than the first (and that's hard to do) both in character development and plot line. The plot line is focused with few subplots to confuse younger readers.<br /><br />It is excellent for all ages and especially the youngest readers. Adults who read to their younger children, beware, because like the first novel, because once you start, you won't want to put it down.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11287235600552111527" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer911301616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14731071634289509947">This book was really awesome. I thoroughly enjoyed it with all of its fairy and mythological creatures. Seth and Kendra are two siblings who discovered that their grandparents were the caretakers of a magical menagerie in the first installment, Fablehaven. In this one, the evil Evening Star is trying to make their move against Fablehaven, and the siblings have to use all their wits and courage to defend the menagerie and the world. Kendra was awesome, smart, motivated, and responsible. She was j</span>
  <span id="freeText14731071634289509947" style="display:none">This book was really awesome. I thoroughly enjoyed it with all of its fairy and mythological creatures. Seth and Kendra are two siblings who discovered that their grandparents were the caretakers of a magical menagerie in the first installment, Fablehaven. In this one, the evil Evening Star is trying to make their move against Fablehaven, and the siblings have to use all their wits and courage to defend the menagerie and the world. Kendra was awesome, smart, motivated, and responsible. She was just as great in this book as in the last one. Seth had more character development. He begins to realize the weight of his actions and that he can't act without thinking it through. New characters are introduced who are quirky and fun and sometimes infuriating but altogether fantastic. The pacing of the story was quick but never too fast, and I was never confused as to what was happening. A tremendous middle grade series so far, I'm excited to read the next sequel. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14731071634289509947" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Almak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Almak" href="/user/show/1148362-almak">Almak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90706662" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15917971207880057867">The events in <i>Rise of the Evening Star</i> pick up months after where <i>Fablehaven</i> left off. It continues the adventures of Kendra and Seth Sorensen as they become embroiled in an insidious plot by the forces of evil to obtain powerful, magical items and unleash a nearly unstoppable horror.<br/><br/>Mull deftly continues to add to the wonders of the world that is Fablehaven, giving the reader new exciting storyline and plots while nimbly threading in those from the previous book.<br/><br/>His writing etches the framework</span>
  <span id="freeText15917971207880057867" style="display:none">The events in <i>Rise of the Evening Star</i> pick up months after where <i>Fablehaven</i> left off. It continues the adventures of Kendra and Seth Sorensen as they become embroiled in an insidious plot by the forces of evil to obtain powerful, magical items and unleash a nearly unstoppable horror.<br /><br />Mull deftly continues to add to the wonders of the world that is Fablehaven, giving the reader new exciting storyline and plots while nimbly threading in those from the previous book.<br /><br />His writing etches the framework of what Fablehaven is and in a "Hitchcock-esque" manner, allows the reader's imagination to fill in that beautiful (and oftentimes deadly) world.<br /><br />The reader is treated to another encounter with the Satyrs, Doren and Newel, and they can't help but make one laugh. I reservedly compare them to Fred and George Weasley of the Harry Potter series, but with enough distinct differences to make them characters in their own right.<br /><br />A better book than it's predecessor, Mull has raised the bar and I eagerly look forward to reading "Grip of the Shadow Plague," the third book in this series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15917971207880057867" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13035055596399809954">All right. This book was a mess. By about page 300 I was just zipping through it, so as to have the vital information for the next installment, because A and C <i>promised</i> it gets better. Sigh. <br/><br/>As usual, Mull delivers on imaginative world building, and the pace never slows, but his logical foundation is so weak I don't dare examine it--one too-direct breath could knock the whole thing over.<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Kendra's fairykind thing really got on my nerves after a while.   <span id="freeText13035055596399809954" style="display:none">All right. This book was a mess. By about page 300 I was just zipping through it, so as to have the vital information for the next installment, because A and C <i>promised</i> it gets better. Seriously, I swear a magic toilet bowl that swallows the Society of the Evening Star and belches peace powder all over the world would be an easier story to swallow than his tidy clean-up jobs. <br /><br />Still very readable, and it will still hold its appeal for the MG crowd, according to my middle-grade correspondent. Please, please let it get better.</span>

<div id="review_8893440" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/8893440" />
    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/611340-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">ANYONE</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8893440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6890975272546636233">GREAT writing. If you liked Harry Potter, you'll LOVE this one. The writing is tighter, the characters not as....angst-filled, a little more real, I think.<br/>The world is so beautiful and yet real-feeling. There is a great sense of morality without the SLAP of it in your face. NO force feeding here, just a delightful romp, jog and then a mad-dash to the climax in a world of majesty and power that is both magical and compelling.<br/>LOVED it. EVERY person (at least a dozen) I have recommended it to (even</span>
  <span id="freeText6890975272546636233" style="display:none">GREAT writing. If you liked Harry Potter, you'll LOVE this one. The writing is tighter, the characters not as....angst-filled, a little more real, I think.<br />The world is so beautiful and yet real-feeling. There is a great sense of morality without the SLAP of it in your face. NO force feeding here, just a delightful romp, jog and then a mad-dash to the climax in a world of majesty and power that is both magical and compelling.<br />LOVED it. EVERY person (at least a dozen) I have recommended it to (even die-hard fantasy-haters) really enjoyed this novel!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6890975272546636233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/1022336-sarah">Sarah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer22159565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18008755724012452657">I think this book was better then the first. I am still not drawn to the main characters. I wish Kendra would take some more initiative and try to find out what her talents and powers are from being made fairy kind. There is so much build up to that and it is left hanging again in this book like it was in the first. I wish Seth would set a better example in the book, he is constantly disobeying, I was not thrilled with the things the children did in this book, i.e. sneaking out of their parents </span>
  <span id="freeText18008755724012452657" style="display:none">I think this book was better then the first. I am still not drawn to the main characters. I wish Kendra would take some more initiative and try to find out what her talents and powers are from being made fairy kind. There is so much build up to that and it is left hanging again in this book like it was in the first. I wish Seth would set a better example in the book, he is constantly disobeying, I was not thrilled with the things the children did in this book, i.e. sneaking out of their parents home to go with a stranger, sneaking out of his grandparents house with someone that could possibly be a traitor, his violent orders to Mendigo when they were being chased by the imps, ect. ect.<br />I found Mull's imagination fun and the story more exciting then the first book. It was fun to read more about the objects within Fablehaven. I would like to hear more about what magical creatures are in Fablehaven, not just the evil ones. Something to make the place sound more magical, and not so evil. <br />I thought it was very ingenious to end the book they way he did with the letter, it makes me anxious to read the third book to find out more. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18008755724012452657" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_487684136" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/487684136" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1629258-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364233070p2/1629258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/487684136?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/1629258-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1629258-erin?shelf=children-teen">children-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1629258-erin?shelf=paranormal-fiction">paranormal-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1629258-erin?shelf=rubbish">rubbish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer487684136" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer880873918155826966">Fablehaven is flat and forgettable. There is plenty of action and adventure, but it is soon forgotten when the book is finished.<br/><br/>However, I did have to give this book the dubious honor of being labeled “rubbish”. Mull has an uncanny knack for writing offensive things about Indians. This book had children playing on a Foosball table populated with cowboys and Indians – complete with headdresses and bare chests. For those struggling to wrap their heads around this, an illustration is included on pa</span>
  <span id="freeText880873918155826966" style="display:none">Fablehaven is flat and forgettable. There is plenty of action and adventure, but it is soon forgotten when the book is finished.<br /><br />However, I did have to give this book the dubious honor of being labeled “rubbish”. Mull has an uncanny knack for writing offensive things about Indians. This book had children playing on a Foosball table populated with cowboys and Indians – complete with headdresses and bare chests. For those struggling to wrap their heads around this, an illustration is included on page 166. Really?! Why couldn’t the figures on the Foosball table just be soccer players in red and blue?- Like on every other Foosball table?<br /><br />My other rant about Mull’s prejudice comments focuses on his use of albinism to mark recipients of a curse. Really? How can this type of rubbish be included in a children’s book? Albinism is a genetic health issue and not the result of magic.<br /><br />Mull’s books seem to be full of offensive and racist comments. He lacks cultural competencies and respect. I am going to start reading book three and I am willing to bet that it has something offensive, most likely about Indians, in it. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="880873918155826966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1091623461" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1091623461" />
    <a title="Mairéad (is roaming the Undying Lands)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9184362-mair-ad-is-roaming-the-undying-lands"><img alt="Mairéad (is roaming the Undying Lands)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472748159p2/9184362.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1091623461?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mairéad (is roaming the Undying Lands)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mairéad (is roaming the Undying Lands)" href="/user/show/9184362-mair-ad-is-roaming-the-undying-lands">Mairéad (is roaming the Undying Lands)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1091623461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11782097463551984818"><i>
  <b>“Sometimes the most preposterous lies are the most believable.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>4 stars.<br/><br/>Certainly an improvement from the first book, but Seth is still an idiot. Kendra has become the most capable out of the both of them, but I can see Seth learning <s>somewhat</s>. I look forward to reading the next book in the series.<br/><br/>Sorry this is such a short review. :P</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2965251078" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2965251078" />
    <a title="Jen (LOHF/Book Den) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1384646-jen-lohf-book-den"><img alt="Jen (LOHF/Book Den) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571332684p2/1384646.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2965251078?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen (LOHF/Book Den) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen (LOHF/Book Den) " href="/user/show/1384646-jen-lohf-book-den">Jen (LOHF/Book Den) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416957706" href="/book/show/1691582.Rise_of_the_Evening_Star">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1384646-jen-lohf-book-den?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1384646-jen-lohf-book-den?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2965251078" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7871595333039723938">Why is this not a movie series?<br/><br/>I'm really enjoying the Fablehaven series. It is just the pick me up I've been needing lately, and I'm having a blast reading this series with my son.<br/><br/>The creatures and the action and the roles of the main characters really kicked into gear in this second installment. I love that the main characters are brother and sister. Brandon Mull writes kids so well.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AwJXPod8DcGXtkOXfOZiKd0eEvyqr6MM6Y2qWF14ZJitLm4vm7X2tGlPSGypSqwUMZ8L85UVw9BS15dwORfi4A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iU3jPjecWQd4BBwpbjLR/+lVCslBnOUuB4hFOnB7DEsnYdovK1Wicob9F9K7nh/CBdQTxn4mhfK80ngSFBSKMw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer10387085482084923451">Brandon Mull resides in a happy little valley near the mouth of a canyon with his wife and three children. He spent two years living in the Atacama Desert of Northern Chile where he learned Spanish and juggling. He once won a pudding eating contest in the park behind his grandma’s house, earning a gold medal. Brandon is the author of the New York Times bestselling <i>Fablehaven</i> series and <i>The Candy S</i></span>
  <span id="freeText10387085482084923451" style="display:none">Brandon Mull resides in a happy little valley near the mouth of a canyon with his wife and three children. He spent two years living in the Atacama Desert of Northern Chile where he learned Spanish and juggling. He once won a pudding eating contest in the park behind his grandma’s house, earning a gold medal. Brandon is the author of the New York Times bestselling <i>Fablehaven</i> series and <i>The Candy Shop War</i>.<br /><br /><br /></span>
